24:824:63132:20:21:108:516:626:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:The recent years of the Permanent Fund payments provide an opportunity to explore 
24:825:63214:21:21:72:522:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:the short-term relationship between income payments and mortality.  Payments were initially 
24:826:63306:21:20:72:517:584:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:made entirely by check, mailed at a rate of 50,000 per week.  Payment by direct deposit was 
24:827:63398:20:21:72:517:564:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:introduced in 1993.  Approximately 30 percent of recipients initially received their dividend 
24:828:63492:21:21:72:517:543:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:this way, which grew to two-thirds of recipients by 2001 and three-quarters by 2006.  Direct 
24:829:63585:21:21:72:520:522:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:deposits are made on only one or two dates, and since at least 2000, over 90 percent of paper 
24:830:63679:21:20:72:513:501:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:checks have been processed and mailed in a single batch shortly after the payment of direct 
24:831:63771:20:21:72:501:481:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:deposits.  The exact dates that direct deposits were paid, as well as the dates checks were 
24:832:63863:21:21:72:522:460:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:issued, are shown in Table 7 for the years 2000 to 2006.  We use the timing of direct deposits 
24:833:63958:21:20:71:520:439:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:from 2000 through 2006 to investigate whether dividend payments change mortality patterns 
24:834:64048:20:21:71:521:419:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:among Alaskans.  We focus on this period because of the popularity of direct deposit and the 
24:835:64141:21:21:71:431:398:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:close proximity between the receipt of direct deposits and paper checks.48  
24:836:64217:21:20:108:518:377:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:The primary data for this analysis are from the MCOD restricted-use files from 2000 
24:837:64301:20:21:72:491:357:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:through 2006, which include decedents’ state of residence.  We create separate weekly 
24:838:64387:21:21:72:508:336:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:counts of deaths for Alaskans and residents of the rest of the United States for periods that 
24:839:64481:21:20:72:413:315:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:include the direct dividend payments and several weeks afterwards.49   
24:840:64552:20:21:108:499:295:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Residuals from a simple regression using these data show an increase in Alaskan 
24:841:64632:21:21:72:505:274:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:deaths at the point of direct deposit payments.  In Figure 4 is the result of creating weekly 
24:842:64726:21:21:72:523:253:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:counts of deaths in each state of residence for annual ten-week periods that begin fifteen days 
24:843:64822:21:20:72:514:232:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:after Labor Day, regressing these counts against week-year dummies and dummies for each 
24:844:64910:20:21:72:497:212:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:state in a negative binomial model of the type used in section 1, and then calculating the 
24:845:65001:21:22:72:521:191:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:mean residuals in terms of when Permanent Fund payments arrive.  Deaths in Alaska deviate 
24:846:65091:22:8:72:218:169:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:                                                            
24:847:65151:8:16:72:497:161:42:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:48 Since 1998, the estates of Alaskans who applied for the dividend in March but died prior to its payment 
24:848:65258:16:11:72:512:145:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:around October have received the full amount.  Using this time period therefore also allows us to rule out any 
24:849:65369:11:7:71:427:134:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:bequest-related “death elasticity” of the sort suggested by Kopczuk and Slemrod (2003). 
24:850:65457:7:16:72:510:127:42:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:49 Alaska has a disproportionate number of aircraft and fishing accidents (Baker et al., 1992).  Fatalities from 
24:851:65570:16:12:72:513:111:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:these events can be significant relative to the number of deaths in Alaska in any single week.  To decrease the 
24:852:65681:12:11:72:518:99:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:variation in weekly deaths, in both the Alaskan and non-Alaskan groups we remove deaths with an Underlying

25:854:65899:0:20:72:518:708:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:most from trends in other states in a positive direction in the week dividends are paid, and in 
25:855:65995:20:21:71:496:688:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:a negative direction two weeks later.  This is consistent with an increase in deaths when 
25:856:66085:21:21:71:496:667:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:income is paid which largely displaces mortality which would have occurred soon after. 
25:857:66172:21:20:108:512:646:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:The econometric model here is a simple difference-in-difference specification, with 
25:858:66256:20:21:72:503:626:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:treatments occurring at particular times of the year in Alaska.  The data for the rest of the 
25:859:66350:21:21:72:507:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:U.S. provides an estimate of the time path that would occur in the absence of the dividend 
25:860:66441:21:20:71:517:584:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:intervention.  Let w denote twelve seven-day periods that begin on Tuesdays,50 with the first 
25:861:66535:20:21:72:510:564:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:period each year beginning fifteen days after Labor Day, the first Monday in September.51  
25:862:66626:21:21:72:524:543:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Let ln(yswy) be the natural log of the deaths for state s (with s=1 for Alaska or s=0 for all other 
25:863:66726:21:21:71:503:522:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:states) in week w and year y.  Dividend(1) is a dummy that equals one the first week after 
25:864:66817:21:20:71:500:501:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:dividend payments are made and zero otherwise, and Alaska is a dummy variable for the 
25:865:66903:20:20:71:279:481:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:state of interest. The model we estimate is:

27:920:71576:0:20:72:189:708:144:Times:144:Times:3.         Discussion         
27:921:71606:20:21:72:522:688:144:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f1: Many authors have demonstrated that consumption increases after individuals receive 
27:922:71691:21:21:72:499:667:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:an expected infusion of cash.  In this paper, we returned to three tests of the LC/PIH and 
27:923:71782:21:20:72:520:646:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:developed two others to document the mortality consequences of this excess sensitivity.  We 
27:924:71874:20:21:72:492:626:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:find that mortality increases after the receipt of income for a wide variety of payments: 
27:925:71964:21:21:72:528:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:transfer payments, paychecks, one-time cash bonuses, and annual residency-based dividends.   
27:926:72057:21:20:108:504:584:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Changing levels of consumption/activity is the most plausible mechanism through 
27:927:72137:20:21:72:490:564:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:which income receipt affects mortality.  The findings for particular causes of death are 
27:928:72226:21:21:72:508:543:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:consistent with this, for both when we observe a relationship – like we do for heart attacks 
27:929:72319:21:21:72:462:522:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:and traffic accidents – and when we do not, as with the tests using cancer deaths. 
27:930:72402:21:20:108:511:501:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Two alternative reasons for such a relationship are improbable.  First, the change to 
27:931:72488:20:21:71:506:481:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:the Social Security payment schedule and the structure of the 2001 tax rebates allow us to 
27:932:72579:21:21:71:500:460:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:rule out within-month or seasonal factors that coincide with income receipt.  Second, the 
27:933:72669:21:20:71:520:439:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:criteria for receiving these payments should not encourage people to improperly record dates 
27:934:72762:20:21:71:513:419:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:of death for financial gain.  Payments to Social Security beneficiaries cease the month after 
27:935:72856:21:21:71:512:398:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:death,55 a deceased applicant's Permanent Fund dividends go to their estate, military wages 
27:936:72948:21:20:71:502:377:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:are already earned and the tax rebates were based on tax returns from the previous year.   
27:937:73039:20:21:108:495:357:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1: Before discussing some implications, it is important to stress that we cannot say 
27:938:73121:21:21:72:472:336:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:anything about whether people are maximizing their own welfare.  Non-smoothing 
27:939:73200:21:20:72:519:315:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:consumption behavior is consistent with a number of utility maximization models, including 
27:940:73291:20:21:72:518:295:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:hyperbolic discounting (Shapiro, 2005).  Moreover, increased mortality does not necessarily 
27:941:73383:21:21:72:515:274:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:reflect contemporaneous poor health: those whose deaths have been hastened by a few days 
27:942:73472:21:21:72:514:253:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:may have been in poor health already, and external causes of death are largely unconnected 
27:943:73563:21:20:72:492:232:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:to short-term variation in a person's health.  At this point it is hard to judge the value of 
27:944:73657:20:21:72:327:212:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:shifting to smaller, more frequent income payments.  
27:945:73710:21:21:108:514:191:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1: It is also difficult to assess the role of income levels and liquidity constraints, as our 
27:946:73801:21:20:72:510:170:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:tests use partially-treated populations.  What is striking, however, is that similar results are 
27:947:73898:20:21:72:514:150:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:found across a wide range of demographic groups, with our tests covering seniors, working-
27:948:73988:21:29:72:528:129:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:age taxpayers, predominantly younger military personnel, and all of the residents in one state.  
27:949:74085:29:8:72:218:100:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:                                                            
27:950:74145:8:0:72:208:92:42:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:55 www.ssa.gov/pubs/10008.html 
28:951:74178:0:20:108:524:708:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:The percentage changes may seem small: mortality for 65 to 69 year olds increases by 
28:952:74263:20:21:71:514:688:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:1.1 percent the week after Social Security checks arrived in 2005 and 2006, while mortality 
28:953:74355:21:21:71:517:667:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:increased by 2.7 percent for those aged 18 to 64 the week the 2001 stimulus checks arrived.  
28:954:74448:21:20:71:470:646:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Relative to general movements in mortality, however, these results are substantial. 
28:955:74532:20:21:107:507:626:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Consider a simple analysis for 65 to 69 year olds in 2005 and 2006.  There are 471 
28:956:74615:21:21:71:517:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:deaths per day among this group, so paycheck receipt increases mortality by 36.3 deaths per 
28:957:74707:21:20:71:501:584:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:week.  In 2005 there were 5,532,900 people aged 65 to 69, so the death rate increased by 
28:958:74796:20:21:71:514:564:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:7.86E-5 (36.3/5,532,900) the week after paycheck receipt.  To demonstrate the significance 
28:959:74887:21:21:71:516:543:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:of this increase, we select a sample of 15,774 adults aged 65 to 69 using data from the 1987-
28:960:74980:21:21:71:524:522:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:1990 National Health Interview Surveys Multiple Cause of Death (NHIS/MCOD) data file.56  
28:961:75069:21:20:72:512:501:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:We regress a dummy variable that equals one if a person died within 365 days of the initial 
28:962:75161:20:21:72:505:481:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:interview on the natural log of family income, a dummy for gender, a set of race/ethnicity 
28:963:75252:21:21:72:514:460:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:indicators, three indicators for education, six indictors for marital status, and a complete set 
28:964:75349:21:20:72:524:439:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:of age and year-of-survey effects.  The coefficient (standard error) on log of family income in 
28:965:75445:20:21:72:502:419:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:this regression is 0.00297 (0.00151).  Assuming that this represents a causal relationship, 
28:966:75537:21:21:72:515:398:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:then these results suggest that in order to produce an decrease in the mortality rate by 7.86E-
28:967:75632:21:20:72:509:377:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:5, incomes in this group would have to increase by 2.65 percent, which is roughly equal to 
28:968:75723:20:21:72:493:357:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:the annual cost-of-living adjustments to Social Security payments over the past decade. 
28:969:75811:21:21:108:518:336:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Estimates for annual payments in Alaska produce a similar story.  In 2000, there was 
28:970:75896:21:20:72:490:315:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:an average of 52.4 deaths per week among Alaskans aged over 18 years.  A 12 percent 
28:971:75980:20:21:72:507:295:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:increase in mortality in one week would result in an extra 6.3 deaths for this group.  In the 
28:972:76074:21:21:72:508:274:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:2001 American Community Survey, reported median household income was $67,090, and 
28:973:76156:21:21:72:498:253:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:the average household had 2.77 members.  Each applicant received a $1,964 dividend in 
28:974:76242:21:20:72:522:232:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:2000, which would have increased average family income by 9.7 percent.  Using similar data 
28:975:76333:20:21:72:518:212:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:from the NHIS/MCOD, the coefficient (standard error) on the log of family income in a one-
28:976:76423:21:21:72:509:191:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:year mortality regression is -0.00077 (0.00021).  Assuming again that this is represents the 
28:977:76516:21:20:72:492:170:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:causal impact of income on one-year mortality, a 9.7 percent increase in income would 
28:978:76602:20:27:72:505:150:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:mortality rates by 7.45E-5.  Multiplying this by the 418,815 adults in Alaska in 2000, this 
28:979:76694:27:8:72:218:123:121:g_d0_f2:121:g_d0_f2:                                                            
28:980:76754:8:16:72:497:115:42:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:56 This file provides mortality information for National Health Interview Survey respondents by matching 
28:981:76859:16:11:72:515:99:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:surveys to the National Death Index.  A more detailed description of this data set and the sample can be found 
28:982:76970:11:0:72:189:88:100:g_d0_f1:100:g_d0_f1:in Snyder and Evans (2006). 
29:983:77002:0:20:72:482:708:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:increase in income is estimated to reduce deaths by 31.2.  Therefore, in this best case 
29:984:77090:20:21:71:500:688:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:scenario of the impact of income on mortality, the short-term increase in mortality of 6.3 
29:985:77181:21:21:71:481:667:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:deaths eliminates 20 percent of the estimated benefits from Permanent Fund income. 
29:986:77264:21:20:107:507:646:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:These results have implications for research on the socioeconomic determinants of 
29:987:77346:20:21:71:486:626:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:health.  As we noted in the introduction, the authors who have attempted to determine 
29:988:77432:21:21:71:525:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:whether there is a causal impact of income on health have generated inconsistent results.  The 
29:989:77527:21:20:71:522:584:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:short-term mortality impact of income receipt suggests two things about this literature.  First, 
29:990:77624:20:21:71:503:564:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:authors must distinguish the time period of analysis because the short-term consequences 
29:991:77713:21:21:71:506:543:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:may be very different from the long-term consequences.  Second, the short-term mortality 
29:992:77802:21:21:71:495:522:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:effect of income receipt makes it more difficult to use exogenous variation in income to 
29:993:77891:21:20:71:519:501:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:identify a causal link between income and health.  This increases the size of the sample or of 
29:994:77986:20:21:71:479:481:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:the income shock required to find a statistically precise income/health relationship.   
29:995:78074:21:21:107:496:460:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:The results outlined above also suggest a potential mechanism for the pro-cyclic 
29:996:78155:21:20:71:515:439:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:nature of mortality that is outlined in Ruhm (2000).  The estimates in Ruhm and subsequent 
29:997:78246:20:21:71:523:419:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:papers isolate a contemporaneous correlation between mortality and measures of the business 
29:998:78338:21:21:71:491:398:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:cycle; yet to date, little has been offered to explain the pathways producing this result.  
29:999:78430:21:20:71:501:377:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:However, if income rises over the business cycle, then the short-term mortality effects of 
29:1000:78521:20:21:71:333:357:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:income receipt may provide just such an explanation.  
29:1001:78575:21:21:107:504:336:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:There are potential policy consequences flowing from these results.  First, there is 
29:1002:78660:21:20:71:517:315:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:evidence of worse hospital patient outcomes when there are fewer medical professionals per 
29:1003:78751:20:21:71:517:295:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:patient (Kostis et al., 2007).  The heightened mortality associated with income receipt might 
29:1004:78845:21:21:71:515:274:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:suggest that emergency rooms, hospitals, police, and fire departments should adjust staffing 
29:1005:78938:21:21:71:487:253:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:levels in accordance with predictable high- and low-mortality days.  Our search of the 
29:1006:79025:21:20:71:513:232:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Internet has so far not provided any anecdotal evidence that such adjustments already exist. 
29:1007:79118:20:21:107:522:212:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:Finally, we noted in the introduction that some health researchers have suggested that 
29:1008:79205:21:21:71:497:191:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:a way to reduce inequality in health outcomes across socioeconomic groups is to simply 
29:1009:79292:21:20:71:508:170:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:increase income transfers to low income groups.  The results in this paper indicate that the 
29:1010:79385:20:21:71:524:150:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:benefits of such a policy regime shift are far from certain.  There is little evidence to date that 
29:1011:79485:21:21:71:523:129:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:cash transfers increase health.  In contrast, the results in this paper show that, in the short run, 
29:1012:79586:21:0:71:509:108:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:there is a pronounced negative consequence to cash infusions for a wide variety of groups.
